Local News 2

Large Shipment of Opium Seized on the "Jiangda" Steamer 146

Opium and Morphine Concealed in Syrup Barrels

Customs Officials Thoroughly Investigating the Case

The "Jiangda," a steamer operated by the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company on the Yangtze River route, arrived in Shanghai from Hankou the other day. During the unloading of cargo that evening, dockworkers attempting to steal goods discovered a large quantity of opium and a significant amount of morphine concealed in the syrup barrels being transported on the steamer. A secret report was made to the Customs House, and together with Chinese and foreign detectives from the French Concession Police, they searched warehouse number 16 at Jinliyuan and found 53 large syrup barrels. Except for two barrels that were completely full of syrup, the remaining 51 barrels were all filled with morphine and opium. All of the contraband was seized and temporarily stored in the Customs House warehouse. An investigation is currently underway to identify the main culprits involved in the opium smuggling. The detailed information obtained through investigation is recorded below:

Discovery of Opium: The "Jiangda" steamer arrived in Shanghai at 10:00 AM the other day and docked at the Jinliyuan wharf on the Bund in the French Concession. The unloading of cargo was not completed until 3:15 PM, and all the goods were stored in warehouse number 16. At that time, a group of dockworkers pried open one of the many barrels with iron tools and discovered opium concealed inside. This was noticed, and a secret report was made to the Customs House.

Customs Seizure: After receiving the report, the Customs House immediately dispatched a large team of customs officers to conduct an inspection together with Chinese and foreign detectives from the police station. They indeed found opium fully packed in the syrup barrels and seized all of it, totaling as many as 53 barrels. Except for two barrels that were purely filled with syrup, the remaining 39 barrels each contained 20 catties of opium. There were also 12 barrels of morphine, with a combined value of approximately $1.5 million. After verifying the quantity, they were immediately transported to the Customs House warehouse for temporary storage.

No Consignee Found: After the incident, the Customs House checked the markings P.E.H.T. on the 53 barrels. The customers who came to pick up the goods did not have names or numbers, and they used a bearer bill of lading. Therefore, it was impossible to thoroughly investigate whose goods they were. Furthermore, the opium dealers were quite cunning. They knew that the Yangtze River area was not a sugar-producing region, and they pretended to be customers returning goods, hoping to deceive the inspectors. They initially did not expect their scheme to be ruined by the theft of dockworkers.

Attempt to Claim Reward: Since the incident occurred, there has been much speculation in society. Some say that when the opium and morphine were transported from Yichang to Hankou, an informant disguised as a passenger boarded the "Jiangda" steamer and followed it. When the steamer arrived in Nanjing, the informant disembarked first, took the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway to Shanghai, and then reported to the Customs House. However, whether this is true is difficult to say. But yesterday, someone went directly to the Customs House, hoping to receive a reward of three-tenths of the value of the goods. At that time, the Customs House, for the sake of caution, specifically questioned the person claiming the reward about the markings on the goods to see if they matched. The person claiming the reward was unable to answer. Therefore, the Customs House did not pay the reward.

Steamship Company Investigation: The reporter, in view of the importance of this case, made detailed inquiries to all parties. However, it was never determined who transported the opium. It was said that the main transporter was a Mr. Liu, and the contents were jointly funded by more than 20 major shareholders. This was the third or fourth time it had been transported to Shanghai. Yesterday, according to the person in charge of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, the company was not responsible for the opium because there were shippers and bills of lading from various sources. It was heard that an investigation had been launched in Hankou to find the shipper, and the truth would soon come to light.

Western Media Coverage: The North-China Daily News reported that customs officials seized a large quantity of opium in the French Concession yesterday, worth between $250,000 and $500,000. There were a total of 50 barrels, weighing approximately 145 piculs, or 6 tons. They were escorted by the police of the French Concession and the International Settlement to the Customs House warehouse. The opium appeared to have been transported from Hankou a few days ago, declared as sugar, and delivered to a bank in the city. Initially, no one suspected anything, so it was treated as ordinary cargo and temporarily stored in the French Concession warehouse. Yesterday, when dockworkers went to move it, one barrel fell to the ground and broke open, scattering opium all over the ground. Although there was a layer of sugar on the outside, the smell of opium quickly spread. One dockworker first went to inspect it, and other dockworkers followed, vying to take some. This was noticed by the customs officers, who stepped forward to stop them but were beaten by the dockworkers. They rushed to report to the French Concession Police and the Customs House. When the police arrived, there were already more than a hundred gangsters at the scene, making a lot of noise. The police dispersed them and surrounded the opium barrels. Later, Shi Kushi, the leader of the Customs investigation team, arrived with his men. After inspection, it was confirmed that it was all opium. He summoned five or six cars to transport the 50 barrels in batches, escorted by the French police to the Yangjingbang, and then escorted back to the Customs House by the police of the International Settlement. It was not yet clear last night which steamer transported the contraband. The relevant authorities of the Customs House are currently conducting a thorough investigation. According to the Continental Times, customs officials cracked down on a large amount of opium worth $1 million at the Jinliyuan wharf yesterday afternoon. It was packed in 50 wooden barrels, each weighing approximately 700 pounds. It was unloaded from the "Jiangtian" steamer. A dockworker mistakenly believed it was sugar and broke open a corner of the barrel, intending to steal some, and discovered that it was opium. He reported it to the police. It is said that the opium was loaded onto the steamer in Tongzhou and is estimated to total 430,000 ounces, worth no less than $1 million at a market price of $2.40 per ounce.

Huang Yimei, Son of Martyr Huang Xing, Kidnapped 147

Held Captive by Bandits in Huanglong Mountain

Huang Yimei, the second son of the martyr Huang Xing, is a handsome young man. Four years ago, he went to France and majored in agriculture and forestry in Paris. He returned to China this summer after completing his studies. On his way back, he planned to inspect the land reclamation conditions in North China. Therefore, he set off from Paris in mid-July with three of his friends, returning to China via Siberia. They entered Manchuria, Rehe, Chahar, and Suiyuan, and went to the area west of Baotou, carefully inspecting the land along the way. In early August, they detoured to Lungkwan, intending to transfer to Taiyuan and then return south. Unexpectedly, on the way to Huanglong Mountain south of Hecheng, Mr. Huang and his friends stayed at a farmhouse at the foot of the mountain to examine the soil quality and agricultural products in detail. They were targeted by the mountain bandits, who, on the night of August 22, armed with lights and weapons, captured Mr. Huang and his three friends and took them into the mountains. The bandit leader interrogated them harshly. Knowing that Mr. Huang was a descendant of the martyr, he forced him to write a letter to his family, instructing them to pay a ransom of 20,000 yuan by September 25, otherwise they would be executed. After receiving the letter from Mr. Huang, his family was extremely anxious because the martyr had no inheritance and they could not raise such a large sum of money in a short time. They are now asking for assistance from the families of other martyrs. Mr. Huang has also sent several letters from the bandit den to a certain Central Committee member in Shanghai, begging him to find a way to rescue him and quickly remit the money to Zeng Shize at 35 Shuanglong Lane, Dadongmen Street, Taiyuan (Zeng is Mr. Huang's uncle). Because he is on Huanglong Mountain, he cannot handle it directly. If the money is sent to his home, it is too far from the bandit den.

Lu Ziqing Tragically Shot and Killed by Kidnappers 148

Lu Called for Help After Being Kidnapped

Bandits Shot Him in a Panic

Lu's Energy Weakened, and He Died from His Injuries

The Chauffeur's Life Can Hopefully Be Saved

At around 9:00 AM yesterday, an attempted kidnapping and shooting of the victim occurred near Kunming Road and Liaoyang Road. The details of the incident are recorded below:

Lu Ziqing's Business: The victim, Lu Ziqing, courtesy name Jiupeng, was 48 years old and from Ningbo. He lived at 24 Fen'an Lane, Huade Road, and was the manager of the Huada Foreign Firm at 6 Sichuan Road. He also engaged in real estate and recently established the Huadong Iron Factory at the corner of Zhaobang Road and Kunming Road, hiring technicians to assist with everything. Every morning, before going to the Huada Foreign Firm, Mr. Lu would always accompany his eldest son, Jiankang, 21 years old, in his own yellow Chevrolet car, number 10035, to the factory to inspect it. He personally handled all the affairs in the factory. His chauffeur was Lu Dalong, from Yangzhou, 33 years old.

Bandits Asked for Help with Guns: At around 9:00 AM yesterday, Mr. Lu still accompanied his eldest son and engineer Sun Xuetang in his own car to the factory as usual to inspect it. He was about to leave when Mr. Ding, a foreman, came forward to discuss matters with Mr. Lu. Mr. Lu stopped to talk. After a few words, four thugs suddenly jumped out from outside the door, each holding a handgun, and said to Mr. Lu, "Friends, help us." Seeing that something was wrong, Mr. Lu knew he had encountered kidnappers and quickly jumped into the car. The chauffeur, Lu Dalong, also quickly started the engine and drove off. His eldest son, Jiankang, and engineer Sun Xuetang were fortunate to have been warned by another cement worker and stopped them from going out, thus escaping the disaster.

The Chauffeur Was Dealt with First: The car had not gone more than a few yards when it was chased by the bandits. They intimidated the chauffeur with guns and ordered him to stop. The chauffeur had no choice. Seeing that the bandits were all on foot, he secretly locked the engine so that the car could not move and hid the key in his pocket. When the bandits approached the car, they ordered the chauffeur to hand over the engine key. Lu Dalong replied that it was in the factory and he had to go to the factory to get it. Upon hearing this, the bandits began to search the chauffeur's pockets. Lu Dalong desperately covered his pockets. The bandits drew their guns and fired three shots at his head and waist. The chauffeur immediately fell into the car. One of the bandits got into the car, pushed him to the side of the road, and drove the car westward.

The Victim Shot While Calling for Help: Mr. Lu was guarded by three bandits beside him. Seeing that his chauffeur was injured, he shouted for help in the car. The three bandits covered his mouth. When the car reached the intersection of Binyang Road, Mr. Lu saw a uniformed police officer and two plainclothes detectives coming towards him about 200 yards away. He bravely shouted for help. Seeing that the situation was not good, the bandits fired two shots at the top of Mr. Lu's head, pushed him out of the car, and drove away quickly. The detectives heard the gunfire and saw someone falling out of the car. They rushed forward and saw that Mr. Lu had fallen in a pool of blood, barely breathing. At the same time, Mr. Lu's chauffeur was found nearby. They rushed to send the injured master and servant to Tongren Hospital for treatment and reported it to the Yulin Road Police Station. The police station immediately dispatched personnel to investigate and search for the missing car, which was found near Jiangwan Road and North Sichuan Road at 11:00 AM.

The Master Died, but the Servant Could Still Be Saved: Lu and the chauffeur Lu Dalong were sent to Tongren Hospital by the Yulin Road Police Station. The hospital immediately gave them emergency treatment and found that the bullet was still lodged in Lu's skull, making it difficult to remove for the time being. Due to Mr. Lu's age and weakened energy, he died from his injuries at 5:00 PM yesterday. The hospital reported it to the Yulin Road Police Station. The police station sent the corpse car to the forensic examination office on Feilun Road for examination. Mr. Lu left behind a wife, a concubine, eight sons, and one daughter. His eldest and second sons were born to his first wife. His second son, named Kuan, 15 years old, is currently studying at Guanghua University. The chauffeur Lu Dalong was injured in the face, back, and buttocks in three places but is not in serious danger. The bullet has been removed by the hospital, and his life can hopefully be saved. The police station is paying close attention to this case. After a day of investigation yesterday, they have made some progress.

Kidnapper Urged Fellow Citizens to Love Their Country Before Execution 149

Also Said He Was Ashamed to Be Shot

Asked the Judge Not to Publish It in the Newspaper

Chen Huiging, a kidnapper from Yancheng, 36 years old, was found to have conspired with accomplices to kidnap Yan Yutang, a real estate businessman with number 58 Jiangxi Road, at around 9:00 AM on May 4th of this year, while the victim was riding in his private car number 8967 to an office. He was arrested by Chief Detective Liu Zhaokui and others from the General Police Station and sent to the First Special District Court. After interrogation, he was sentenced to death and reported to the Jiangsu Provincial Government for approval. He was ordered to be executed. Yesterday morning, Judge Shen Puzeng came to the execution court and ordered the police to bring the prisoner Chen forward. He asked if he had any last words and wrote a letter to his family. According to Chen Huqing's confession, he had already written a letter to notify them. Now I have been deceived by evil friends and committed this unfaithful, unfilial, unkind, and unjust act. Therefore, I have placed my parents, wife, and children outside my heart. Only in the police station is there a gold watch worth $70, which I now ask the court to send a letter to my relative Liu Jisheng at number 427 Kangti Road in the French Concession on my behalf. He finished speaking with a bitter smile, lamenting that his mind was already confused and repeatedly touching his forehead with his hand, unable to speak. Judge Shen ordered the Chinese and foreign police to take him down, along with the photos and the entire case file, and escort him to the execution ground of the Second Prison in Caohejing in a car. At the same time, he sent a letter to the local court, instructing Inspector Chen Dai to bring the bailiffs Gu Hanqing, Wang Jianqing, Gao Jinsheng, Zhou Lianghua, and Xiong Dingchen to the execution ground. The prisoner confessed that he was 36 years old and from Yancheng, and requested that a letter be written to Liu Jicheng on Kangti Road, asking him to tell his wife to raise his two-year-old child and never forget his parents-in-law. I am very ashamed to be shot today and ask the judge not to publish it in the newspaper. Our country's national power is declining. I hope that the people of the country will love their country and struggle, etc. The official ordered the execution, and the execution bailiffs took the prisoner down for execution. The body was taken away by the hall for collection.

County Government Holds Agricultural Product Competition 150

The Shanghai County Government recently received an order from the Jiangsu Department of Industry, which was forwarded from the Ministry of Industry, stating that holding agricultural product competitions could allow farmers to observe and compete, and improve agricultural methods. In a blink of an eye, the autumn harvest and slack farming season are approaching, which is the right time to hold the competitions. It is ordered that the county immediately follow the competition regulations issued by the former Ministry of Agriculture and Mining. The county government immediately ordered the county farm yesterday to prepare to hold the competition and report the methods and dates in advance.

Silk Factory Strike Expanded, Concession Area Joined the Strike 151

The Fulun Silk Factory Strike Was Quickly Resolved

Party and Government Agencies Sent Personnel to Mediate

More than 9,000 female workers in the silk factories in Hongkou suddenly announced a general strike the day before yesterday morning. Party and government agencies are sending personnel to investigate and mediate. Unexpectedly, yesterday, the silk factories in the three districts and the Fulun Shuanggong Silk Factory at the end of Tianbao Road also joined the strike, and the situation is quite serious. The details are recorded below:

Continued Strike: About 12 silk factories in the Hongkou district, such as Chengxiang Chengyuanfeng, etc., with more than 9,000 female workers, requested an increase in wages and a reduction in working hours. Since the general strike was announced the day before yesterday morning, all work in the factories has been completely stopped. Yesterday, the factories did not sound their whistles, and most of the female workers stayed at home, waiting for a resolution. A reporter from the Dagong Daily went to inspect each of the factories yesterday afternoon and saw that work had stopped in each of the factories and there were no workers gathering in front of the factory gates. The situation was quite quiet. The factories still insisted on refusing the demands. Otherwise, they would rather open the factory.

Three Districts Joined: Yesterday morning at 2:00 AM, many female workers at the Yuyuan Silk Factory on Guoqing Road prevented workers from entering the factory, so only 60% of the workers went to work. Seeing the tense situation, the factory owner released all the female workers in the factory. After leaving the factory, the female workers went to the Chuxin Silk Factory on Manzhou Road and continued to the Longyuan Xuxiang Jingwei Runchang and other silk factories on Arabassatur Road. The female workers of each factory automatically stopped working and went out to join the strike. The factories also stopped work. At that time, the order was in chaos throughout the area. The police station immediately sent Chinese and foreign detectives to suppress the situation. The Silk Industry Union of the Three Districts sent personnel to persuade the workers. The female workers put forward four conditions: (1) Restore wages of six cents, (2) Working hours must not exceed eleven hours, (3) Reissue the previously deducted big ocean subsidies, and (4) Restore the Sunday reward. The union representative promised to submit a petition to the party and government to negotiate with the capitalists. It was not until 8:00 PM that the female workers began to disperse gradually.

Submit Petition to Party and Government: After accepting the demands of the female workers, the Silk Industry Union of the Three Districts sent representatives Yang Shumei and others to submit a petition to the party and government agencies requesting approval. The original petition is as follows: The matter is about requesting the quick dispatch of personnel to mediate the matter. The meeting reported that the factory did not comply with the mediation decision of July 8, deducting big ocean subsidies, which almost caused a labor strike. Later, the meeting repeatedly persuaded the workers and submitted a petition to your bureau, requesting that the factory be ordered to fulfill the mediation decision. After several months of delay, on the 20th of this month, after your department mediated, it was decided that work would start at 6:00 AM and end at 6:00 PM. The wages of the car washer were increased, and the previously deducted big ocean subsidies were investigated and reissued, etc. However, at a time when the price of silk in this factory was more than 200 taels higher than when the mediation was done on July 8, not only was the wage not increased, but it repeatedly failed to comply with the decisions of the two mediations on July 8 and the 20th of this month. The working hours were ostensibly in compliance with the mediation on the 20th of this month, with work starting at 5:40 AM, but secretly extending the afternoon work time to 6:40 PM. Therefore, the daily working hours have not been shortened, and are still the same as before the second mediation. Therefore, all the workers are unable to bear it, and the strike that has been brewing for several months broke out this morning, and proposed (1) restoring the original wage amount, (2) working hours must not exceed eleven hours, (3) reissuing the previously deducted big ocean subsidies, (4) restoring the Sunday reward and increasing the wages, and other conditions, requesting the union to negotiate to achieve the goal. This area's silk factory owners have always been difficult to reason with, and a special document is submitted to report it. It is hoped that personnel will be dispatched quickly to mediate to avoid the expansion of the labor strike. This is indeed a virtue. Respectfully submitted to the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau.

The Fulun Disturbance Subsided: Since the female workers in the silk factories in the entire Hongkou area went on a general strike the day before yesterday, the female workers of the Fulun Shuanggong Silk Factory at the end of Tianbao Road did not join because their treatment was different from that of the single-worker silk factories. Unexpectedly, starting yesterday morning, all 400 female workers in the factory suddenly announced a strike. The reason was that the factory had repeatedly dismissed workers without reason, so the female workers expressed dissatisfaction. Yesterday, the factory suddenly dismissed four female workers again, which aroused the anger of the workers, so they announced a strike starting in the morning, demanding the reinstatement of the four dismissed female workers. After hearing the news, the Silk Industry Union of the Fourth District sent two representatives, Dong Xingen and Lu Xusheng, to mediate. As a result, the capitalists agreed to reinstate the four dismissed female workers. The female workers also believed that the goal had been achieved and decided to resume work today.

Jiucheng Strike Failed: Yesterday, at noon, when the female workers of the Jiucheng Silk Factory on Changan Road in Zhabei were dismissed from work, all the female workers gathered at the factory gate to discuss the matter, demanding an increase in wages and intending to strike. The situation was very serious. Fortunately, Wu Suzhen and others were sent by the Silk Industry Union of the Sixth District to persuade them, so it was not realized. However, when work started in the afternoon, all the female workers were still unwilling to enter the factory. Therefore, the work start time was about an hour later than usual. According to the person in charge of the union, who told the Dagong Daily reporter, the union has now sent personnel to do their best to persuade the workers to wait for the resolution of the three or four districts. The union will then negotiate with the capitalists based on reason. In short, within the scope of the union, during this serious period, a labor strike will never be allowed to occur.

Party and Government Sent Personnel to Investigate: Since the female workers in the silk factories in the Hongkou district had a strike, the party and government agencies in this city, because the matter was serious and needed to be handled urgently, sent Zhou Lianze, a staff member of the Civil Training Section of the Municipal Party Committee, and Wang Xianqing, the director of the Mediation Section of the Third Section of the Social Affairs Bureau, to the Silk Workers' Union of the Fourth District to investigate and solicit opinions because the strike had expanded and could not be mediated for a while, so they immediately returned to the bureau to report, intending to discuss solutions and then proceed with the handling.

Municipal Authorities Order Telephone Company to Cease Repair of Underwater Cables 156

The American-owned Shanghai Telephone Company installed telephones in various districts of Pudong in this city, using underwater cables buried in the Huangpu River to connect with Puxi. Recently, the cables were damaged, and water entered the lines, rendering them unusable. The company previously failed to report to the Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities, the responsible authority, and privately dispatched workers for repairs, which the Bureau promptly stopped by instructing the Public Security Bureau's water patrol team. Subsequently, the company submitted a form requesting permission to proceed with the work. However, the Bureau of Public Utilities, citing the company's repeated delays and evasions regarding the already signed temporary contract draft, and its lack of legal basis for operating and repairing equipment within the city, did not grant permission. Yesterday, it was learned that the company had sent a letter to the Bureau of Public Utilities, stating, in essence, that if permission to repair the cables was not granted, the Bureau should be held responsible for the impact of the delay in restoring public services. The Bureau, regarding this as a result of the company's delay in signing the contract, responded severely, stating that the company should bear full responsibility. It also instructed the water patrol team to maintain strict surveillance throughout the night to prevent the company from secretly repairing the cables and urgently submitted a report of the situation to the Municipal Government for review. The Bureau's letter to the telephone company is excerpted below: "To the Shanghai Telephone Company: Your letter of the 23rd of this month has been received. It is noted that your company has not entered into any contract with this Bureau or the Shanghai Telephone Bureau of the Ministry of Communications. Your company has no legal basis for installing or repairing any telephone equipment within this city. This Bureau has no obligation to issue licenses to your company, and this Bureau has the right to weigh whether or not to issue them. If any impact arises from the delay in restoring public services, it is entirely the result of your company's delay in formally signing the temporary contract draft signed on October 23rd of last year, and your company should bear full responsibility. The statement in your letter that this Bureau should be responsible is without basis. This letter is in response for your information. Respectfully, [signed] Bureau of Public Utilities."

Nationals Successfully Manufacture Wireless Transmitting Machine 157

Power Reaches Central United States

Since its establishment, the Chinese Amateur Radio Society in this city has actively promoted science and aroused public interest in research. Its members are located throughout the country, most of whom are engaged in the wireless radio industry. Society member Lu Zengqian recently manufactured a small, less than five-watt transmitting machine. Using shortwave amateur radio station call signs, it has reached the central United States (Coleridge Province), 11,000 miles from Shanghai. He also manufactured a transmitting machine of less than one watt, which can communicate with Japanese amateur radio stations and has recently reached San Francisco in the United States. This amateur radio station, call sign AC8ZT, has communicated with more than 300 amateur radio stations in countries around the world. It is reported that these gentlemen have more than ten years of experience in this research.

Closing Arguments Heard in Day and Night Bank Director Lawsuit 158

Verdict Scheduled for Afternoon of the 28th

In the case of the collapse of the Shanghai Day and Night Bank's Great World Amusement Savings Department, the former French Court ruled to partially reject the claims against Ye Shantao, while Zhao Qinbo, Zhou Songqing, Chen Xingwu, and others were held responsible as directors and shareholders. Subsequently, the creditors, dissatisfied with the portion of the judgment concerning Ye Shantao, retained lawyers Wang Shizong, Yan Luqing, Chen Zhibi, Dong Yu, Jiang Yiping, and others to file an appeal with the Third Branch of the High Court, seeking to confirm Ye Shantao's responsibility as a director and shareholder. Zhao Qinbo, Zhou Songqing, Chen Xingwu, and others also appealed the initial judgment of the former French Court, retaining lawyers Yang Zhihao, Lu Shaozong, Zhang Shizhao, Wu Zhiping, and others to request the High Court to overturn the original judgment. These developments have been reported in various newspapers. Yesterday afternoon, the Civil Division of the Third Branch of the High Court, presided over by Division Chief Zhao Zhenhai, along with Judges Guo Dezhang and Fan Peien, held a hearing in Civil Court One. All parties involved were represented by their attorneys. The court first briefly questioned each of the attorneys and then ordered the commencement of arguments. Attorney Yan Luqing, representing the appellants, stated that the facts of the case had been clarified by the presiding judge and requested that the court proceed in accordance with the appellant's request. The arguments of the other attorneys representing the creditors, including Wang Shizong, were similar. Wu Zhiping, representing Zhou Songqing and Chen Xingwu, argued that his clients held positions as consultants to the Gongfa Company and received monthly "husband and horse fees." They were neither directors nor shareholders and requested that the original judgment be overturned and the claims of Jing Xiren and others be rejected. Ye Shantao was represented by lawyers Lu Shaozong and Zhang Shizhao, who argued that although their client, Ye Shantao, had previously been a director of the Gongfa Company, he had declared his resignation in 1922, which was announced in the newspapers. As for the 200 shares of stock under Ye Shantao's name, they were transferred to Ge Songxuan in September 1930. Since Ge is present and can testify, and Ye had already resigned, why does Ye Shantao's name still appear in the new board of directors roster from 1928? Lawyer Lu replied that this was likely a mistake by Huang Chujiu, but that all the account books presented were Huang's one-sided records. The court then questioned witness Ge Songxuan, who stated that he was from Hangzhou, sixty years old, and that in September 1930, Ye Shantao transferred 200 shares to a merchant, with a face value of 2,000 yuan, for a price of 1,000 yuan. The merchant bought them because he saw the potential for profit. At that time, he wanted to transfer the shares at the Gongfa Company, but the transfer was stopped because it was dividend time. This was the truth. Zhao Qinbo's son, Zeng Yu, represented by lawyer Yang Zhihao, stated that the initial judgment held Zhao Qinbo responsible as a director, but Zhao was neither a director nor a shareholder. He was merely a close friend of Huang Chujiu and assisted him in various matters, for which he received monthly compensation. He requested that the original judgment be overturned. After reviewing the statements, the court announced the conclusion of arguments and scheduled the verdict for 2:00 PM on the 28th of this month. The court adjourned as the clock struck eight.

Arson Follows Theft to Destroy Evidence 160

Yang Quanfu's Extreme Cruelty

Xia Hehai, a carpenter from Pudong, lived in an unmarked rural bungalow on Qianjiatang in the French Concession along Avenue Joffre. He left for work at 6:00 AM the day before yesterday. His neighbor, Yang Quanfu, a fellow villager and plasterer, knew that Xia was away and conceived an evil plan. He dug a hole in the wall from his house and entered Xia's house, stealing clothes, ornaments, and cash worth over 80 yuan. Neighbors noticed the fire and extinguished it with water, preventing a major disaster. When Xia returned home, he was informed by his neighbors and reported the incident to the police station. Detectives, along with Wen Zhi, went to the scene for investigation. Yang was not at home, but he was apprehended when he returned home at midnight. Under interrogation, he confessed to the crime. Police lawyer Gu Xixi stated the details of the case, saying that the defendant's arson and theft were extremely heinous. Fortunately, neighbors noticed and extinguished the fire, preventing a major disaster. The police are prosecuting him for endangering public safety and theft under Articles 187 and 338 of the Criminal Code. However, the police investigation is not yet complete and requested a one-week extension for further interrogation. Yang Quanfu admitted to the theft and arson without denial. Initially Engaged to Miss Cai, Then Cohabited with Miss Li

Recently Infatuated with a Prostitute, Miss Li Has Now Filed a Lawsuit

Fang Jiali, 22 years old, resides in Zhengdeli, South Chengdu Road, and possesses a large fortune. He is still studying at a certain university. He was initially engaged to a Miss Cai, but then became involved with Li Sanyuan (21 years old), a graduate of Suzhou Changhai Women's School from Wumen. They rented a house and cohabited. The lawsuit stated, in essence, that it was a case of abandonment and seduction and requested severe punishment according to the law, as well as an attached private prosecution. The lawsuit alleged that in the spring of 1930, the defendant coveted the plaintiff's beauty and colluded with Zhu Lianyuan, a fellow villager of the plaintiff, to shower her with flattery and lure her to No. 27 Xicheng Lane, Ximen Road. They falsely claimed that he was not yet married and asked Zhu to act as a matchmaker to marry the plaintiff as his wife. That night, they held a banquet to entertain the matchmaker. During the banquet, the defendants planned to intoxicate the plaintiff. They then opened room 225 at the Dongfang Hotel and forcibly raped her while she was mentally dazed and unable to resist. The next morning, he introduced her to his mother, Fang, and uncle, Fang Yixin, to show that he was not deceiving her. He then claimed that since they were husband and wife, they should cohabit, so they settled in No. 12, Guifuli, Taiping Bridge. On May 17th of that year, the plaintiff suffered from severe vomiting. The defendant suspected that she had caught a cold and instructed his concubine (i.e., Fang) to accompany her to Dr. Fang Jiacheng's clinic in Yehuali, Tongfu Road, for treatment. After Fang diagnosed her as pregnant, the entire Fang family was extremely happy. Fang instructed the plaintiff to move to No. 38, Juxingli, Beitidali Road, so that they could visit each other day and night. Meals were provided at the defendant's uncle Fang Yixin's house. They then moved to the defendant's own residence at No. 25, Zhengyuanli. On December 21st of that year, the plaintiff gave birth to a daughter, and the defendant's mother was even more pleased, naming her Meidi. Clothes and items were purchased by Fang. Since then, the relationship between the two sides has become even more affectionate. In the first month of 1932, the defendant suddenly looked worried and said that he had been engaged to a Miss Cai in his youth and that she would imminently sue if he did not marry her. He asked for forgiveness and asked to marry Miss Cai first and the plaintiff later. If she could help him through this crisis, he would never forget her kindness. The plaintiff, seeing the defendant's sincerity, agreed to save him. After the defendant married Miss Cai, they still lived in peace. However, the defendant was greedy and insatiable. Soon after, he had an affair with Fengjun Laqi of Shantou Road. The plaintiff, seeing the defendant's unbridled behavior, went to Fengjun's place to inquire and tried to dissuade him, and told his mother. However, the defendant suddenly turned against the plaintiff because she was preventing his actions, urging her to marry someone else and ignoring her. He also stopped paying for her living expenses. The act of raping a woman while she is mentally incapacitated and unable to resist constitutes a crime under Article 202, Section 1 of the Criminal Code. Deceiving someone into believing that they have a marital relationship and engaging in joint adultery constitutes a crime under Article 244 of the Criminal Code. Furthermore, the second and third defendants designed to help the first defendant seduce the plaintiff and commit adultery, which constitutes a crime under the same Article 244. The plaintiff requests that the court arrest and severely punish them according to the law to uphold morality and order the first defendant to pay the plaintiff a one-time sum of 30,000 yuan for living expenses. It is hoped that this will be approved. After receiving the complaint, the court will reportedly schedule a hearing soon.

Subsequently, a letter was sent to the Bureau's Western Supervisor, who arrested Qian and sent him to the Jiading Road Police Station before handing him over to the First Special District Court. Yesterday morning, Judge Fu Lin conducted an investigation at the Criminal Division Four. Police lawyer Zhang Tianyin stated that the order to move the vendors in the Wuzhou Road vegetable market upstairs was indeed issued. Later, the vendors requested the Health Bureau to cancel the decision. The (Nong) Western official wrote a letter to the director, canceling the previous proposal on the 7th. The vendors paid the money on the 9th. According to (Nong), he had not seen the defendant since he went on leave. The Western official was present in court and requested to be questioned. According to (Nong), he was British and an inspector at the Pingliang Road Health Bureau. At the time, the vendors went to the office and talked to the defendant, and he knew a little. However, the money obtained by the defendant was not handed over to him. When questioned, Qian Guisheng insisted that the order to relocate the vendors was issued on the 5th. At that time, the vendors went to the office to request help. Nong said he would find a way. On the 7th, the director ordered the cancellation of the order. He then asked him to go to the Wuzhou Road vegetable market to collect the money. In the afternoon of the 9th, (Nong) had his chauffeur drive to the court, picked him up, and handed over the money near the entrance of the court. He had only been working at the Health Bureau for two weeks. The Western official called him foreman. Police lawyer Zhang said that the defendant's attitude was unrepentant and questioned the Western official for a long time. Considering the situation, (Nong) was very suspicious, but the defendant did not have the ability to embezzle the money. The crime of dereliction of duty charged by the police seemed illegal and requested a lighter sentence, suggesting that the defendant was a dupe. The defendant also retained lawyer Zheng Wenkai to defend him. The court questioned each of the vendors whether they wanted to recover the money they had worked hard to earn. They replied yes. Judge Fu then sentenced Qian Guisheng to a fine of 200 yuan. If he could not pay, he would be imprisoned at a rate of three yuan per day. The number of days of detention would be offset by three yuan per day. He was ordered to return 222 silver coins to the vendors and post a 500-yuan bond for release.

Soap Factory Worker Dies Tragically 166

Xie Qijin Falls into Boiling Pot and Scalded to Death

Xie Qijin, 21 years old, a native of Qingjiang, worked as a worker in the China Soap Factory at No. 231 Yangshupu Road. At 2:30 PM the day before yesterday, he was working next to a soap-boiling pot when he accidentally fell into the pot. At that time, the temperature of the soap material being boiled in the pot reached as high as 160 degrees Celsius. Although the foreman, a British national named Muller, and colleague Ning Wengui were nearby, they were unable to save him. After being pulled out, he was badly burned beyond recognition. After being notified, the Yangshupu Police Station ordered detectives to investigate and transferred the body to the Fielun Road autopsy station. Yesterday morning, they reported to the First Special District Court, which sent prosecutor Guo Wei, forensic officer Wang Zudian, and others to the station to examine the body. During the public hearing, the witnesses testified that Muller, a British national, said that the deceased was standing on a wooden board next to the pot. The pot contained two kinds of soap-making materials. The deceased was adjusting the rod inward when the boiled liquid suddenly rose and fell into the deceased's eyes, causing him to fall in. Ning Wengui testified that he and the deceased were working together at the scene, and the Western foreman was also there, ordering them to work quickly, so the deceased was anxious and fell in. Xie Qiao, the deceased's mother, testified that she was 68 years old and usually depended on the deceased for support, so she requested that the factory provide generous compensation. After hearing the testimony, Guo ruled that the deceased Xie Qijin had died from being scalded while alive. The body was handed over to his mother, Xie Qiao, after signing a bond, for burial. The factory representative agreed to give the deceased's mother a compensation of 400 yuan.

The Huashang Taishan Insurance Co., Ltd. at No. 2 Beijing Road in this city officially opened yesterday. It operates in various types of insurance, including life, fire, and accident insurance. Beekeeping Industry Initiates Research Society 168

The Chinese beekeeping industry has always been unorganized. Now, the Dongfang Beekeeping Company, Zhonghua Beekeeping Company, Fengsheng Farm, and others, which have achieved success, have decided to organize the Chinese Beekeeping Research Society because they believe that in this time of national crisis, it is not enough to promote industry without research in order to survive and improve. The purpose of the society is to study beekeeping and honey production. It is reported that they have rented the fourth floor of No. 96 Beijing Road as the society's office and will soon begin recruiting members. Comrades, whether they are already beekeepers or not, are welcome to join. Those who pay attention to industry can join and explore.

Railway Decadal Publication is Responsible for Transportation Special Issue 171

A Compilation of Opinions from Various Experts

All Railway Administrations are Selling on Consignment

The Railway Decadal Publication, edited by Zheng Baozhao, has been greatly improved in terms of content and appearance since it was published this year. The number of sales has increased sharply, reaching far and wide. It is a periodical publication with the most innovative ideas in the domestic railway academic community. The Ministry of Railways is promoting responsible transportation in order to enrich people's livelihoods. The publication has specially collected the opinions of various experts on this issue, detailing the advantages and disadvantages and the handling procedures, for the research of railway staff and all sectors. The book is finely bound in one volume, totaling more than 10,000 words, divided into the following columns: Editorial, Special Articles, Research, Records, Laws and Regulations, Investigation, and Railway Chronicle. It is set as the combined edition of the 8th to 11th issues of the publication. Important catalogs are as follows: The Economic Value of Responsible Railway Transportation (Zheng Baozhao), Responsible Transportation and Reorganization of Railway Administration (Yu Yan), The Meaning and Implementation of Responsible Railway Transportation (Tan Yaozong), A Review of the Past Preparation of Responsible Transportation and Future Efforts (Xu Chuanyin), The Main Points of the General Rules for Responsible Railway Car Transportation (Tan Yaozong), Three Major Issues in Implementing Responsible Transportation (Tan Yaozong), The Handling Methods of Responsible Railway Transportation (Yang Ge), The Problem of Railway Transportation Responsibility and Compensation Claims of Merchants (Xiong Dahui), etc. The attached General Rules and Bill of Lading Regulations are especially convenient for reference. The special issue retails for two dimes. The full year, 36 issues, only sells for a fixed fee of eight corners, including postage. The publishing house is at No. 686, Kangleli, Kang Nao Road, Shanghai, and the Beixin Bookstore and various railway administrations.

Huafa Golden Ear Company Entertains the Medical Community 181

It is well known that white fungus is a tonic, but few know that there is a rare golden ear. On the evening of the 23rd, Mr. Fan Fayuan, the owner of Huafa Golden Ear Company, hosted a banquet to entertain famous doctors in this city. Dozens of famous doctors, including Xie Liheng, Zheng Qihao, Song Guowei, Zhang Zanchen, and Ren Nongxuan, attended. During the banquet, golden ears were served, which were fat, beautiful, and rich, and more abundant than white ears. This product comes from the roots of thousand-year-old pine trees on the Wannan Snow Mountain in Lijiang Prefecture, Yunnan Province. It is shaped like Ganoderma lucidum and its color is like gold, hence the name golden ear. The company sends people to serve samples every day, charging only ten yuan per month, which is a small amount to obtain the supreme treasure, which is much cheaper than milk and other products.

Letter 183

To the Editor of Shen Bao,

Sir,

I am writing to you on behalf of my client, Mr. Zhu Binkui (formerly Bingkui), who claims that he read in the Shen Bao on the 12th of this month that Bingkui was posing as an investigator, claiming that Bao Muxian and others had dug up graves and defrauded foreigners of 300 yuan, and that he had reported it and ordered the police to investigate. He was shocked. Bingkui has now entrusted a lawyer to inquire, and Bao Muxian said that he did not know Zhu Bingkui, so how could he have defrauded foreigners of 300 yuan? He thinks that the investigator's investigation was inaccurate, and because the matter concerns his reputation, he entrusted your lawyer to write to your newspaper to correct the matter in order to avoid misinformation.

I am writing to you with the facts and hope that you will correct the matter.

Yours respectfully,

Lawyer Zhou Yu, June 24th

Rumor of Mexico Changing to the Gold Standard: Yesterday's Spot Gold Price Rose Even More Vigorously, but with Intermittent Weather, the Retraction Was Still Not Large. In the Morning and Afternoon, It Was Still Seven Taels Higher, but in the End, It Continued to Rise by Five Taels. Initially, the Silver Market Declined, but It Was Not Affected. In Fact, the Futures Market of the Silver Exchange Declined and Weakened. The Stock Market Was Small and Then Large Again, so the Morning Opened Flat. Sellers Showed Courage and Immediately Fell. Melting Good Malpractice in Silver Furnaces Is Prohibited 190

According to News From the Financial World Yesterday, the Silver Furnace Bought the Good Malpractice of British and Dragon Dollars, etc., at a Price Increase for Profit, and Placed It in Lu Yang to Turn It Into Silver. Because the Foreign Li Has Been Falling Recently, Exceeding the New Price of Historical Special Lows, the Individual Interest Is Very High, so They Bought and Melted It One After Another. Now It Has Been Visited by the Government, Thinking That This Melting Will Inevitably Lead to the Disappearance of Good Malpractice in the Market, Which Greatly Hinders It. Cotton Yarn Market Sentiment Leans Bearish 192

The cotton yarn market experienced a morning dip followed by an afternoon rise, but the overall trend is weak. Due to unfavorable conditions, most are inclined towards a bearish outlook. Actual demand in the market is increasingly quiet, and all sectors lack vitality, except for Rongxing, which maintains a bullish position and remains unmoved. In summary, the base price has already reached a medium level. Shanghai factories have relatively depleted their existing yarn stock, leading to a shortage of newly released yarn. However, generally, people believe that although the harvest is abundant this year, the price of rice is too low, making it difficult for farmers to achieve significant economic prosperity. Consequently, there is less hope for robust yarn sales in the future, and the sentiment remains bearish.

People's Standard Drops Below 50 Taels

The People's Standard market opened with a decline due to another drop in American cotton prices, leading to an increase in sellers. Market sentiment loosened, with each contract falling by one, two, three, or four cents. By the afternoon closing, the market generally tightened, with each month rebounding by five or six cents. The total transaction volume for the day was 36,250 bales. The sales breakdown is as follows: Dachang sold 2,500 bales, Changfeng 1,400 bales, Shenji 1,200 bales, Tongsheng 550 bales, Zhijin Yukang 1,000 bales, Yuanda 850 bales, Shenda 850 bales, Xiesheng 1,000 bales, and Jifeng 600 bales. American Cotton Initially Fell and Then Rose Last Week 197

Heavy Rains in Mississippi and the West

New York, September 23rd: A report on the cotton market conditions this week states that raw cotton prices initially fell and then rose due to purchases by the public and short covering. Hedging activity has decreased compared to before, and speculative long positions seem to have been largely closed. Short sellers have been accumulating, and upon seeing a gradual decrease in cotton sales and a surge in buying interest, they became apprehensive. The reason for the strong buying interest is the report of heavy rains in the Mississippi River basin, rain in various parts of the East, and storms in the West. This is expected to delay the listing of new cotton and damage already open cotton bolls. Private reports mentioning the inferior quality of new cotton are still circulating. Some say that the cotton yield in the first half of September is even worse than the usual situation for the entire month. However, some also predict that the peak of new cotton listing activity will occur before mid-October, as last year, the period with the most new cotton listings and the lowest cotton prices in the fall was in early October. Hedging transactions have now decreased, and it is reported that several cotton farmer groups are stockpiling their cotton. The weekend statistics are recorded below (in thousands of bales):

Grain Market in Northern Shanghai: Rice Prices Trend Weaker 198

Southern Market Not Opened Due to Disputes

Southern Shanghai: Yesterday, the rice supply from various sellers reached approximately 1120, but the stock in Pudong was limited. Due to a sudden dispute between the rice merchants and the measuring clerks, the workers stopped measuring, and the goods ready for sale had to wait until the dispute was resolved before they could be measured.

New Zha: Yesterday, 56 ships arrived from inland areas. Transactions in both urban and rural areas were sluggish. Kunshan and Yixing rice prices were each down by 20 cents, and the price of new Yangdu Jian rice was also down by nearly 10 cents. Changshu and Wuxi early japonica rice prices were stable, while new japonica rice and new guest japonica rice prices were unchanged. However, water caltrop rice was scarce and sold quickly, stabilizing the opening market.

Fuzhou Sellers Attempt to Stock Hunan Zhejing Rice 199

Imported Rice Sales Slow and Slightly Weak

Yesterday, the imported rice market remained uninterested. Local business was less than 1,000 bags, and prices showed a slight decrease of 5 cents. However, sellers remained firm and unwilling to lower prices significantly. Due to sluggish sales and the continuous arrival of new rice, it is difficult for the situation to improve without large-scale customer demand. Yesterday, 300 bags of small-milled rice were sold at 8.60 yuan, and 100 bags of old small-milled rice were sold at 8.37 yuan. 500 bags of Saigon No. 1 rice were sold at 9.40 yuan. There is not much Hunan rice in the market, about 1,000 bags of Zhejing rice, with a price difference of about 1 yuan, making it difficult to match. Therefore, sellers are unwilling to sell their existing stock. Yesterday, Fuzhou sellers purchased 150 bags of Hunan Zhejing rice at 7.55 yuan.

Standard Flour Market Stabilizes 200

Yesterday, after the opening of the flour market in the morning and afternoon, the prices for each month generally seemed to stabilize. Although the quoted price of imported wheat was slightly lower by about 10-20 cents, the gold price rebounded sharply, and the exchange rate fell. Additionally, although the factories had confirmed orders for imported wheat, they did not try to sell to make money. However, customers were unmoved, and outsiders were aware of the situation, so everyone observed and waited, pushing against each other. Due to the absence of sellers, a few speculators made small purchases, which slightly strengthened the market. However, the total transaction volume for the day was only 190,000 bags, reflecting the quiet market. Future trends will depend on the attitude of the factories. As a result, the price for this month was 0.25% higher than the previous day, October was 0.5% higher, November was 0.75% higher, December was 0.1% higher, January was 0.75% higher, and February was 0.5% higher.

Wheat Futures Continue to Fall 201

Yesterday, after the opening of the wheat futures market in the morning and afternoon, the prices for each month continued to fall due to the continued decrease in the quoted price of imported wheat by about 10-20 cents. Factories continued to confirm orders for imported wheat, which naturally made the position of domestic wheat similar to last year. Therefore, most large sellers of No. 43 wheat continued to close out their positions. As a result, all market prices were unfavorable. Fortunately, there were not many new short sellers, so the decline was slightly less severe. As a result, this month was down 0.3%, October was down 0.3%, November was down 0.1%, December was down 0.2%, January was down 0.1%, and February was unchanged. The spot wheat market has become quiet again. Only 300 bags of Yaowan wheat were sold at 3 taels, 5 qian, and 2 fen.

North-South Goods: Red and Black Dates Debut 203

One Falls, One Rises

Recently, new red and black dates have been arriving on the market. Nearly 1,000 bags of Tianjin cotton red dates have arrived in Shanghai. As a result, both customer and self-operated goods have suffered losses, mainly because the dates are damp and soft, making it difficult to maintain the price. Few first arrivals here are sold at 8.5 to 8 taels. The market price yesterday was reduced to 7 taels. The price of new Jixin red dates in the Hankou market is 9 taels, and traders bought some and sell them at 12 taels. The new black dates this year are of good quality. The first few dozen bags were sold at 8 to 8.5 taels. Since then, 200 bags of customer goods and dozens of bags of self-operated goods have arrived. A small amount of customer goods were sold, with high-quality goods at 8 taels and slightly lower-quality goods at 7 taels and 6 qian. Stockholders are unwilling to lower prices further and plan to raise them to 8.5 taels. Free Talk

Random Thoughts on Life 210

— Ji Ping

Recently, this publication has been favored by fellow writers, and submissions have been particularly enthusiastic, with very elegant writing. Could this delightful trend be an unexpected result of the changes in this publication's goals? We express our gratitude for this. This special issue focuses on modern life. We did not prepare for it in advance, as we unintentionally discovered several articles describing "life" in many submissions. Remembering that life is a serious and urgent issue in modern society, Juanweng suggested compiling a special issue on "Modern Life."

Speaking of the hardships and complexities of life, I believe that no nation's people can compare to the Chinese. Our Chinese people's lives are truly bizarre and a spectacle of ancient and modern times. A mixed bag of narratives includes the decadent lives of high-ranking officials, the impoverished lives of scholars, the hellish lives of disaster-stricken refugees, and the lives of laborers treated like beasts of burden. During this time of national crisis, there are also the lives of compatriots in occupied territories living as slaves, the bloody lives of the Northeast volunteer army, and the fiery lives of civilians in war zones. These countless life scenarios range from the blissful experience of ascending to heaven to the miserable existence of being in hell! How can a small number of people enjoy temporary comfort while billions languish in disaster and famine? Isn't this the crime created by politics? We originally hoped for the early success of the revolution, allowing the masses to work with dedication and enjoy their fruits. How could we know that the current situation would be like this, with no hope of improvement!

Who would want to live this subhuman life? Who doesn't want to enjoy comfort? However, comfort is always something for the distant future. As a weak nation, we only hope for coarse clothing and simple food, where everyone can live and work in peace, without foreign aggression or internal conflicts. That would mean our collective life is resolved. Now that the national crisis is increasingly urgent, with survival hanging by a thread, we hope that a few privileged people will have a heart for helping the world, supporting the vulnerable and rescuing the needy. Don't just seek personal security, but think of the masses; the merit will be immeasurable! Consider the universally admired Gandhi. His daily life consists of bread and goat milk for sustenance, simple clothing, bare feet, spinning yarn, and praying as regular activities. How many people in the world can match his great ideals, words, and deeds? May the officials and people of our nation be firm, patient, and resilient, taking Gandhi as their master, always mindful, and acting like the sages of old, "Worrying about the world's troubles before the world does, and enjoying the world's pleasures only after the world has."

A Plea from Life 211

— Shazhou

The World is Cold and Uncaring

First, let's look at the lamentations of impoverished singers in this era of deformed capitalism: "Fire camp, fire camp, faintly red, Grandpa carries water to sell shallots, Grandma churns batter for paper lanterns. Son falls ill and becomes a quack doctor, Daughter-in-law carries a bag to catch lice. Poor today, poor tomorrow, picking up brass and copper." Next, we see the burden of farmers: "Singing a song while transplanting rice, This year's harvest will fill the granary. The ox exerts effort, the ox eats grass, Officials eat rice, I eat chaff. Even the mice want a share of the grain." It's all about the country being poor and the people suffering, with the endless internal strife of warlords, which then produces: "Airplanes fly in the sky, cannons pass on the ground, Trains carry soldiers, carts carry fodder. The rich live in foreign buildings (villagers call foreign concessions foreign buildings), the poor dig cave dwellings." The continuation of natural disasters and wars, coupled with heavy taxes and levies, how can rice not be expensive? Look at "Droughts and floods make rice expensive, The poor suffer. Vegetable roots and tree bark, who cares about their taste? Beggars can beg for food, but the poor can only watch. No work to do, and people still scold them for being lazy." Thus, the poor have no work to do, leading to widespread unemployment. If they lose their jobs, don't they need to eat? But "No money in their pockets, they walk like wandering souls." Try to reason with people, but the world is cold and uncaring, so "When people are poor, they become thin and dark. Borrowing fifty cents, they get nothing. Turning back, people treat you like a thief." If they can't borrow money and can't get food, what can they do? Find "Guanyin powder" (fine clay) to eat. But it causes bloating and can't be eaten, but how can they endure hunger and cold? So, unimaginable crimes are committed one after another. Are these all their own choices?

The times give folk songs the above voices. How moved are we to hear them? But this is precisely what the powerful and wealthy hate. So they close their eyes, and the radio will never broadcast the cries of suffering.

A List of Living Expenses in the Capital 212

— Xi

It is Not Easy to Live in Chang'an

Since the government moved south and Nanjing became the capital of the country, the laws of economics of supply and demand caused prices of goods, food and housing to all increase. Though there is no CPI to compare, roughly, it can be estimated that living cost is five times higher than ten years ago, and ten times higher than twenty years ago.

Civil servants who rely on salaries to live, since the national crisis, get very little income, which is hardly enough to maintain the most basic standard of living. How much the living expenses will amount to for each family becomes information that people would like to know. Here is a most minimal example.

The conditions for this most minimal example are: (1) Small family size, (2) few social engagements, (3) not modernized, (4) at most hire one maid to live thrifty lives. On the other hand, it must also (5) maintain some dignity, and not degrade to begging.

Government Employee Family Expenses Chart

Amount in Yuan

A. Rent 20.0 Roughly 14% on the high side

B. Food 40.0 Roughly 28% on the high side

C. Clothing 15.0 Roughly 11% on the low side

D. Education 15.0 Roughly 11% on the low side

E. Daily Sundry Expenses 25.0 Roughly 18% on the low side

Divided into (1) water bill 2 yuan (2) electricity bill 2 yuan (3) Snacks alcohol and cigarettes 6 yuan (4) Cosmetics 3 yuan (5) stamps 2 yuan (6) toothpaste, towel, toilet paper, matchsticks, paper and writing materials 3 yuan (7) Transportation 3 yuan (8) Summer mosquito coil and fan, winter coal fire, and other sundry expenses average 4 yuan

F. Maid Salary 4.0 Roughly 2.8% on the high side

G. Entertainment 8.0 Roughly 5.7% on the low side

H. Gifts and Donations 13.0 Roughly 9.5% on the low side

Total 140.0 Yuan (100%)

From the chart, entertainment only takes 5% of the expenses, and gifts are double the expense of entertainment. This is already at a minimal level. Which government employee's gift expenses don't exceed one-tenth of income? Monthly clothing expenses are only 15 yuan which are not enough for the whole family to buy shoes and socks. So the wives have to sew two pairs of cloth shoes for themselves. Food expenses are 40 yuan for a family of five. That is an average of 8 yuan per person. Outside meals will cost 12 yuan. Cooking at home is more economic. The rent of 20 yuan can only get you an old flat. Renting a new foreign style house will cost at least 70 yuan. The necessary expenses add up to 140 yuan. Only civil servants with senior positions have this income. For military officers, unless they are major generals, they cannot reach this income. How can the small clerks live?

Sigh!

A Reporter's Life - Fragments 213

— ·Wang· Ding· Jiu

|The Uncrowned King's Realm|

I am just a nameless nobody in the world of journalism. So I call myself a small reporter, (Mr. Hesheng, please forgive my cheeky self-appointment). In my short experience, I feel that being a reporter is both possible and impossible. Now I present my personal experiences as fragments for the benefit of society, so that people can understand a corner of a reporter's life.

X X X X

A reporter's stomach is sometimes wide, sometimes tight. When there is food, it's nights of banquets in several places, Chinese banquets and Western meals, eating until one is bloated. When there's nothing to eat, one must serve the public on an empty stomach. One has to understand the stale leftovers and swallow them down. It really echoes the common saying: "When there's food, eat it hot. When hungry, starve to death."

X X X X

Reporters are like children's toys. When great figures, organizations, and businesses need publicity, they are treated as honored guests and entertained with wine and food. When they are useless, they are tossed aside. If you try to approach them, the great figures block you, organizations close their doors, and merchants shake their heads.

X X X X

Reporters return from attending divorce cases in court, facing difficult dilemmas. The slightest bias or exaggeration will result in either the plaintiff cursing and scolding or the defendant getting angry. Meeting outside the court, the fashionable ladies are most impolite, cursing "kill a thousand times," even scolding "little devils"! Alas!

X X X X

Reporters fear news censors the most. After exerting all their energy to gather information, the results are unilaterally deemed unsuitable for publication. When the censor deletes something important, it feels like a prisoner being sentenced to death, filling one with resentment.

X X X X

A reporter's wife is the unluckiest. After marriage, she doesn't get to enjoy any conjugal pleasures because a reporter's life means working late into the night, leading to a life of solitude as if she were a widow. Returning home at midnight, his wife wants to chat, but he is already asleep like a log. She can only sigh in vain. Therefore, my conclusion is: Reporters are not uncrowned kings at all; they lead miserable lives!

Hong'er's Old Ox 214

— ·Shen· Zhen· Yue

|A Scene from Rural Life|

It was dusk, and the blood-red sun in the west was about to temporarily bid farewell to everything in the world. Crows and magpies were singing goodnight songs in the woods, facing the setting sun. At this time, everything should be resting. Hong'er led his old ox, its work for the day completed, singing mountain songs all the way home.

He and the old ox arrived at their home. As usual, he tethered the old ox under the fruit tree at the corner of the threshing ground, fed it some grass, and turned to go inside. Before he even entered, he heard the little black dog barking wildly inside the door. He knew there must be a stranger who didn't usually come. He hurried inside and saw Uncle Xu from the village in front, the local bailiff, and two uniformed policemen.

·····································

"Uncle Xu, you understand, the fields have been barren for several years. Paying seven *shi* of rice, we don't even have enough to eat porridge. Fertilizer money is indispensable. The rice we borrow in the spring costs eighteen or nineteen yuan per *dan*. When we take the new rice we harvest to the city to sell, each *dan* is only worth seven or eight yuan. The money from selling two *dan* of new rice isn't even enough to pay back the debt of one *dan* of white rice. Where do you think we can get money to pay rent and taxes? If we pay the rent and taxes, we'll have nothing to eat or wear. To be honest, we only eat two thin bowls of porridge a day, and even that's hard to manage." Hong'er's father said to the bailiff.

．　··································································

"Who cares if you eat porridge or rice? If you have money, you can pay. If you don't have money, we'll go see the county magistrate together," one of the policemen warned Hong'er's father.

··········································

"Sir, please forgive me. I really don't have money to pay the rent and taxes right now. When the harvest is better, I'll pay it all off," Hong'er's father pleaded with the policeman.

···································································

"Who cares if you have a good harvest or not? Since you don't have money, come, come, come... let's go together," one of the policemen said.

Hong'er's father pleaded bitterly, and Hong'er's mother and Hong'er also wept and begged for mercy. But tears and snot couldn't replace money. In the end, the police still dragged Hong'er's father away.

································

It was getting late, and the sunlight was gone. The old ox under the fruit tree had eaten its fill. Hong'er and his mother were still sitting on the doorstep, crying. They hadn't even had any porridge, and their stomachs were growling loudly, as if they were also complaining.

···································································

The next morning, Hong'er's mother led the old ox to the city.

·············································································

Night fell again, and Hong'er's father and mother both returned, but the old ox was nowhere to be seen.
