*Shen Bao* Local Supplement

Say

Research on Fasting 215

— ·Fo

Fasting, which means not eating rice or bread, is a passive and boring method. Unexpectedly, it has recently become popular like a bargain, which is quite strange.

What I don't understand is that, according to doctors, a physically strong person will definitely die if they starve for seven days, or at least five. If people like me, who don't eat much normally, would be even less able to withstand it. Suppose I fasted for three days, I would definitely die. According to the acting president of the Indian National Congress, Gandhi can probably survive fasting for twenty-five days, but if he fasts for ten days, there is fear that he will never recover. Yet, the Nulands fasted for over ten days the other day and didn't die. Perhaps there is a way to fast? Someone said that fasting only means not eating rice and bread, but other things can be eaten. If so, then eating things like milk and eggs every day would seem to prevent starvation forever. Fasting would become just a formality. Since I don't want to fast and don't need to study fasting methods, I know that many things in the world are not easy to do. Even just fasting is something that not everyone can do.

Although fasting is popular for a time, the extent of its effectiveness is very different. For example, when the Nuland couple fasted for more than ten days the other day, various important people, due to ideological connections or international relations, rushed to rescue them, exchanging letters and telegrams. As a result, they were able to avoid death and even had the hope of a pardon. This is a relatively effective form of fasting. The second case is the workers of the Sanyou Industrial Company, who, because their request for resumption of work was not granted, all went on a fast. As a result, they not only failed to achieve their goal but also provoked a paper war in the newspapers between general major entrepreneurs and the Central Civil Movement 指委會, with no results. According to a dispatch from Pune yesterday, since Gandhi's fast, many Indians have begun to fast to express their sympathy for Gandhi and his political views. It is also said that Gandhi is now on the third day of his fast and there is now a glimmer of hope, because Solavia, after visiting Gandhi this morning, announced that the issue of the right to participate in politics for the untouchables can be finally resolved today. If this is the case, then Gandhi's fast has unexpected results?

What I don't understand even more is that Gandhi, apart from being frugal and self-disciplined, doesn't have any amazing achievements to speak of. However, even while fasting, he still continues his daily routines of spinning and praying. From this alone, we can see that Gandhi's spirit of hard work, perseverance, and indomitable spirit has been completely revealed. In the past, Zeng Wenzheng made it a rule to write for one hour every day, even when military affairs were pressing, and he never stopped, eventually achieving great success. Now, seeing Gandhi's fast, I am even more aware that the calm attitude of great men and their achievement of great deeds cannot be achieved by mere luck. Jesus has his own reasons too.

Literature and Art

Autumn Day Musings 216

— ·Feng· Nai· Jun

A chorus of metallic sounds fills the air, a lament for the declining glory of the Yellow Emperor. Hunanese bandits are still preparing their arrows, while puppet officials are again taking the stage. I regret not having the strength to cross the river and recover lost territories, and I am ashamed to entrust my patriotism to mere writing. How can I warm myself with even a small mat now? I truly need to taste danger nine times to test my courage.

Snatching Rice Bowls 217

Summoning souls to the sea corner, dark maple forests dim, a single stream, the Wusong River, cuts through the dusk shadows. Eastern lands stir dust, the vast sea turns shallow, old friends, the moon falls, roof beams deepen. Empty thoughts of *乌柏* contrast with dark hair, yet facing yellow flowers, a faint white heart. Life and death, across millennia, evoke many feelings, the desolate sound of the flute in the mountains.

Science

Making Alcohol from Wood 218

— ·Shao· Liang

Everyone knows that alcohol is made from starch, but few have seen alcohol made from wood.

Page 23

But we must understand that everything that was impossible in the past has now become commonplace, right? Making alcohol from wood may become very common in the near future, and there will be no need to be surprised. Because this is not only already successfully tested, but the cost is also very low, which is something that our country urgently needs to manufacture. So, the method of making it is written below:

Making alcohol from wood is successful by utilizing a chemical action. There are originally many ways to make it. One of them is to first use a bucket, fill it with very fine wood chips, and then steam these wood chips with steam for one hour. Then put concentrated sulfuric acid in the wood chips to make it expand, and it gradually becomes a starch-like paste compound and dissolves. Then put a lot of cold water in this dissolving liquid and heat it to 120 degrees Celsius, and it becomes glucose. Add a small amount of alkali to this sugar and, after neutralization, add yeast to make it ferment. Then put this solution in another bucket with holes to allow the liquid to flow down. This flowing liquid is alcohol. Another method is to put dilute sulfuric acid in the wood chips and heat it to a very high temperature, then it becomes glucose. Then use the same method as above to make this sugar, and it can also be turned into alcohol.

In addition to the above two methods, there is also a method of treating wood with strong hydrochloric acid. When strong hydrochloric acid is put into the wood, the cellulose in the wood is acted upon by the strong hydrochloric acid and turns into glucose, from which alcohol can also be made.

How can wood be made into alcohol? This is because the main component of wood is cellulose, and cellulose is formed by the aggregation of starch. If acidic substances are put into this cellulose, a chemical reaction will occur, turning it into glucose, and then making alcohol from this sugar is easy.

Social Improvement Discussion Group

Qualifications Question 219

— ·Jian· Lou· Lou

In such a large society with an excess of people, the demand for talent for positions is absolutely greater than the supply. As the pursuit of bread increases day by day, the supply of bread is only decreasing day by day. Therefore, employers have no choice but to use qualifications as a passive restriction in the selection and use of service personnel (to limit the quantity by quality). As a result, obtaining qualifications has become a prerequisite for finding work. In addition to the introduction and promotion of big figures and the accumulation of wealth for operations, one can surely obtain a superior position without any qualifications. Even for a meager meal, it seems that one must have certain qualifications to get a share.

Nowadays, qualifications are mostly used as the criterion for selecting talents from administrative offices to general public service agencies, and even ordinary larger companies and shops. In some places, qualifications are simply used to determine the level of positions and the amount of salary. For example, a famous large printing house in our country obviously divides employees into different levels, such as doctors, masters, foreign students, domestic university graduates, and vocational school graduates, to determine salary amounts, and cannot cross the line. It implicitly proclaims the prohibition of (those without qualifications do not enter our doors). However, the so-called qualifications here have become narrow and only refer to academic degrees.

Here, I am reminded of the examination system in our country. Considering the original meaning of the examination, it should of course be to select true talents and practical knowledge as the main purpose, but in fact it is the opposite. Often, the regulations for recruitment clearly stipulate the qualifications of candidates at the beginning, and the examination of academic degrees and inspection of diplomas are the first step in the examination procedure. As long as the qualifications are met, the verification is passed, and you can sneak through. As for academic knowledge and experience, you can ignore it, and the so-called oral and written tests are just formalities. For example, lawyers in our country must, according to explicit regulations, pass a formal examination to obtain a lawyer's certificate and perform their duties. However, looking at the thousands of lawyers across the country, almost none have formally passed the examination, because only obtaining a graduation certificate from a foreign university or a legally registered law school in China can allow one to enjoy the preferential treatment of (selection). Putting aside the fact that the selection system clearly contradicts the examination system, under the banner of selection, the general mixed qualifications can safely pass for true, while the general real scholars who have devoted their lives to the study of law are forever excluded from the ranks of elimination due to not meeting the regulations of selection. Can this be said to be a fair approach?

Although, if we carefully analyze the original meaning of (qualifications), it originally contains two meanings: (qualifications) are an internal condition, referring to true academic knowledge and experience, and (form) is an external condition, referring to academic degrees, diplomas, and work experience, etc. Therefore, when discussing qualifications, both should be taken into account, and there should be no bias. When selecting talents, it is better to choose qualifications and give up form when necessary, which is in line with the true meaning of talent selection. However, in modern society, those who have both qualifications are indeed rare, so those with form but no qualifications fill society as much as possible and take great advantage everywhere, while those with qualifications but no form have become discarded and hit walls everywhere. Remember that someone on (Life) once shouted (suffered the loss of qualifications to the full), we know that in this vast world, those who suffer the same disease as someone are not known to be many.

I think this is a problem that deserves attention. The current social (emphasizing form over qualifications) is a morbid state of abandoning the root and pursuing the branch, and there is an urgent need for reform. This column is dedicated to improving society, so I dare to express my humble opinions in a haphazard manner. However, regarding reform plans, my personal knowledge is limited, and I dare not rashly propose them. I sincerely hope that all compatriots can come together to discuss them, so that we can obtain a correct and practical solution. That is the original intention of my clumsy work (throwing a brick to attract jade).

A Corner of Society

In a Small Teahouse 220

— ·Yun

Night revealed its black shadow, shrouding the entire world. The autumn wind was blowing, and the street lamps cast their dim yellow light. Although the scene was bleak, the streets began to liven up, filled mostly with people who looked like workers.

Upstairs in a small teahouse facing the street, the sound of gongs and drums began to ring. The entrance was lit by brilliant electric lights, reflecting some seductive words: (This teahouse tonight specially invites XXX, etc., to sing XXX.)

So, this teahouse swallowed up many of these workers. They came to enjoy this new autumn evening after a day's work. For three hundred coins for a ticket, they could have a pot of tea and listen to local opera.

This low-level pleasure seems to occupy a part of their entire lives. Dance halls, movie theaters, and cafes, these urban civilized pleasures that require money, they would never think of stepping into.

The lively sound of gongs and drums resounded throughout the quiet universe of this autumn night. The sharp singing of women and the strange flirting of men and women on stage all constitute the unique characteristics of this entertainment venue.

The blue smoke, like clouds and fog, filled this popular theater. The audience's laughter and noise were also characteristic of this place.

The warm air was filled.

After half past eleven, the theater closed, and the quiet streets became lively again. A large group of spectators poured out of the teahouse and walked home in the silvery moonlight.

Their hearts were filled with satisfaction, and they discussed who did well and who did poorly in groups of three or five on the road.

The slightly cold autumn wind blew, but they did not feel cold.

School Photographs 221

Secrets of Exams 222

— ·Hui· Jun

For those who have been to school, exams are a necessary hurdle. There are entrance exams for admission, monthly exams, quarterly exams, and also temporary exams, quizzes, and final exams of various kinds. Therefore, to cope with various difficult challenges, students who read books but don't forget entertainment and read books but don't forget love, rack their brains and carefully design schemes to deceive teachers and get scores and credits, so that they can graduate, and report to their parents.

There are methods of cheating, as the saying goes, (magicians all know how to perform tricks, but each has their own skills). To summarize, there are no less than the following types:

Distracting the Tiger from the Mountain: It is difficult for the teacher to supervise the exam, but it is difficult to guard against. For example, A and B collude. A deliberately asks the teacher to explain the test questions, diverting his attention, and B takes the opportunity to copy from here and there, or turn the book to copy the hidden items, displaying skills.

Division of Labor and Cooperation: Beforehand, agree with the classmates sitting in front, behind, left, and right, that A is responsible for Chapter 1 of a certain course, and B is responsible for Chapter 2. After the work is assigned, everyone works hard and prepares carefully within their defense zone, increasing the night shift. If the test questions are in A's territory, A will send someone to help other classmates, and the same will be done in B's territory.

Standing Guard: As soon as the test paper is distributed, immediately send a copy to a classmate waiting outside the exam hall. After receiving it, he asks a classmate of a higher grade to do it. After the answer is done, make a ball of paper, and when the teacher is not paying attention, make a wink and throw it in. If the teacher sees it, he can refuse to accept it, and there is no handle to find.

Dual-Purpose Hat: When encountering exams, you often see several classmates wearing baseball caps, because on the one hand, when stealing a look at the book, the gaze is downward, making it difficult to detect, and at the same time, hidden items can be placed in the hat, pretending to scratch the head and think, and you can steal a look at everything.

All Kinds of Hidden Items: Hidden items come in all shapes and sizes, some are just outlines, and after reading the title, you can associate with the content. These are made by students who are more willing to study. Students who do not study copy many things in tiny characters, but they are all irrelevant things. I once saw a classmate who wrote words on a blank piece of paper with a needle. On the surface, there was nothing, but the effort spent was really not small. There are also those who imagine things, write the hidden items on foreign paper, and tie them to the belt with a rubber band. When the teacher comes, they automatically hide it in a hurry.

The Secret of the Sleeves: The sleeves are the most convenient for hiding items.
